<p>The <b>Mediterranean Sea</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Sea" title="Sea">sea</a> connected to the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a> and almost completely enclosed by land: on the north by <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>, on the south by <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, and on the east by the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>. The Sea has played a central role in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Western_civilization" title="History of Western civilization">history of Western civilization</a>. Although the Mediterranean is sometimes considered a part of the Atlantic Ocean, it is usually referred to as a separate body of water. <a href="/wiki/Geological_Evidences_of_the_Antiquity_of_Man" title="Geological Evidences of the Antiquity of Man">Geological evidence</a> indicates that around 5.9 million years ago, the Mediterranean was cut off from the Atlantic and was partly or completely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desiccated" title="Desiccated">desiccated</a> over a period of some 600,000 years during the <a href="/wiki/Messinian_salinity_crisis" title="Messinian salinity crisis">Messinian salinity crisis</a> before being refilled by the <a href="/wiki/Zanclean_flood" title="Zanclean flood">Zanclean flood</a> about 5.3 million years ago.
</p><p>The Mediterranean Sea covers an area of about 2,500,000 km<sup>2</sup> (970,000 sq mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> representing 0.7% of the global <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">ocean</a> surface, but its connection to the Atlantic via the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>—the narrow strait that connects the Atlantic Ocean to the Mediterranean Sea and separates the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>—is only 14 km (9 mi) wide. In <a href="/wiki/Oceanography" title="Oceanography">oceanography</a>, it is sometimes called the <i>Eurafrican Mediterranean Sea</i>, the <i>European Mediterranean Sea</i> or the <i>African Mediterranean Sea</i> to distinguish it from <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_sea_(oceanography)" title="Mediterranean sea (oceanography)">mediterranean seas</a> elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The Mediterranean Sea encompasses <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_in_the_Mediterranean" title="List of islands in the Mediterranean">a vast number of islands</a>, some of them being of volcanic origin. The two by far largest islands are <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>.
</p><p>The Mediterranean Sea has an average depth of 1,500 m (4,900 ft) and the deepest recorded point is 5,267 m (17,280 ft) in the <a href="/wiki/Calypso_Deep" title="Calypso Deep">Calypso Deep</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a>. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/30th_parallel_north" title="30th parallel north">30°</a> and <a href="/wiki/46th_parallel_north" title="46th parallel north">46° N</a> and longitudes <a href="/wiki/6th_meridian_west" title="6th meridian west">6° W</a> and <a href="/wiki/36th_meridian_east" title="36th meridian east">36° E</a>. Its west–east length, from the Strait of Gibraltar to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Iskenderun" title="Gulf of Iskenderun">Gulf of Iskenderun</a>, on the southeastern coast of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, is about 4,000 kilometres (2,500 mi). The north–south length varies greatly between different shorelines and whether only straight routes are considered. Also including longitudal changes, the shortest shipping route between the multinational <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Trieste" title="Gulf of Trieste">Gulf of Trieste</a> and the Libyan coastline of <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Sidra" title="Gulf of Sidra">Gulf of Sidra</a> is about 1,900 kilometres (1,200 mi). The water temperatures are mild in winter and warm in summer and give name to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">mediterranean climate</a> type due to the majority of precipitation falling in the cooler months. Its southern and eastern coastlines are lined with hot deserts not far inland, but the immediate coastline on all sides of the Mediterranean tends to have strong maritime moderation.
</p><p>The sea was an important route for <a href="/wiki/Merchant" title="Merchant">merchants</a> and travelers of ancient times, facilitating trade and cultural exchange between peoples of the region. The <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Mediterranean_region" title="History of the Mediterranean region">history of the Mediterranean region</a> is crucial to understanding the origins and development of many modern societies. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> maintained nautical hegemony over the sea for centuries.
</p><p>The countries surrounding the Mediterranean in clockwise order are <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>; <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> are island countries in the sea. In addition, the disputed territory of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus" title="Northern Cyprus">North Cyprus</a>, and some enclaves, notably <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>, have coastlines on the sea. <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> is the largest coastal settlement. The drainage basin encompasses a large number of other countries, the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a> being the longest river ending in the Mediterranean Sea. 
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Mediterranean_region" title="History of the Mediterranean region">History of the Mediterranean region</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_civilizations">Ancient civilizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ancient civilizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AntikeGriechen1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1616" data-file-width="2836" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AntikeGriechen1.jpg/390px-AntikeGriechen1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AntikeGriechen1.jpg/585px-AntikeGriechen1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AntikeGriechen1.jpg/780px-AntikeGriechen1.jpg 2x" width="390"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AntikeGriechen1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Greek (red) and Phoenician (yellow) <a href="/wiki/Colonies_in_antiquity" title="Colonies in antiquity">colonies in antiquity</a> c. the 6th century BC</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1614" data-file-width="2534" decoding="async" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/390px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/585px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/780px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png 2x" width="390"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> at its farthest extent in AD 117</div></div></div>
<p>Some of the world's greatest ancient civilizations that were the base of the entire Western culture were located around the Mediterranean shores and were greatly influenced by their proximity to the sea. It provided routes for trade, colonization, and war, as well as food (from fishing and the gathering of other seafood) for numerous communities throughout the ages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the shared climate, geology, and access to the sea, cultures centered on the Mediterranean tended to have some extent of intertwined culture and history.
</p><p>The most notable Mediterranean civilizations in classical antiquity were the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_state" title="City state">city states</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persians" title="Persians">Persians</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phoenicians" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a>, both of which extensively colonized the coastlines of the Mediterranean. Later, when <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, the Romans referred to the Mediterranean as <i><a href="/wiki/Mare_Nostrum" title="Mare Nostrum">Mare Nostrum</a></i> ("Our Sea"). For the next 400 years, the Roman Empire completely controlled the Mediterranean Sea and virtually all its coastal regions from Gibraltar to the Levant.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darius_I_of_Persia" title="Darius I of Persia">Darius I of Persia</a>, who conquered Ancient Egypt, built a canal linking the Mediterranean to the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>. Darius's canal was wide enough for two <a href="/wiki/Trireme" title="Trireme">triremes</a> to pass each other with oars extended, and required four days to traverse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, the archaeological team of experts from Underwater Research Center of the <a href="/wiki/Akdeniz_University" title="Akdeniz University">Akdeniz University</a> (UA) revealed a <a href="/wiki/Shipwreck" title="Shipwreck">shipwreck</a> dating back 3,600 years in the Mediterranean Sea in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. 1.5 tons of copper <a href="/wiki/Ingot" title="Ingot">ingots</a> found in the ship were used to estimate its age. The <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Antalya" title="Governor of Antalya">Governor of Antalya</a> Munir Karaloğlu described this valuable discovery as the "<a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe" title="Göbekli Tepe">Göbeklitepe</a> of the underwater world”. It has been confirmed that the shipwreck, dating back to 1600 BC, is older than the "<a href="/wiki/Uluburun_shipwreck" title="Uluburun shipwreck">Uluburun Shipwreck</a>" dating back to 1400 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages_and_empires">Middle Ages and empires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Middle Ages and empires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> collapsed around 476 AD. Temporarily the east was again dominant as Roman power lived on in the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> formed in the 4th century from the eastern half of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. Another power arose in the 7th century, and with it the religion of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, which soon swept across from the east; at its greatest extent, the Arabs, under the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyads</a>, controlled most of the Mediterranean region and left a lasting footprint on its eastern and southern shores.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">Arab invasions</a> disrupted the trade relations between Western and Eastern Europe while disrupting trade routes with Eastern Asian Empires. This, however, had the indirect effect of promoting the trade across the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>. The export of grains from <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> was re-routed towards the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">Eastern world</a>. Products from East Asian empires, like silk and spices, were carried from Egypt to ports like <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> by sailors and Jewish merchants. The <a href="/wiki/Viking_expansion" title="Viking expansion">Viking raids</a> further disrupted the trade in western Europe and brought it to a halt. However, the <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norsemen</a> developed the trade from Norway to the <a href="/wiki/White_Sea" title="White Sea">White Sea</a>, while also trading in luxury goods from <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Spain</a> and the Mediterranean. The <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire_under_the_Isaurian_dynasty" title="Byzantine Empire under the Isaurian dynasty">Byzantines in the mid-8th century</a> retook control of the area around the north-eastern part of the Mediterranean. Venetian ships from the 9th century armed themselves to counter the harassment by Arabs while concentrating trade of Asian goods in Venice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1341" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a>, 1571, ended in victory for the European <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1571)" title="Holy League (1571)">Holy League</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Turks</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimids" title="Fatimids">Fatimids</a> maintained trade relations with the <a href="/wiki/Italian_city-states" title="Italian city-states">Italian city-states</a> like <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Amalfi" title="Duchy of Amalfi">Amalfi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoa</a> before the Crusades, according to the <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Geniza" title="Cairo Geniza">Cairo Geniza</a> documents. A document dated 996 mentions Amalfian merchants living in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>. Another letter states that the Genoese had traded with <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>. The caliph <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ma%27ad_al-Mustansir_Billah" title="Ma'ad al-Mustansir Billah">al-Mustansir</a> had allowed Amalfian merchants to reside in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> about 1060 in place of the Latin <a href="/wiki/Hospice" title="Hospice">hospice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a> led to flourishing of trade between Europe and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outremer" title="Outremer">outremer</a></i> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Genoa, Venice and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Pisa" title="Republic of Pisa">Pisa</a> created colonies in regions controlled by the Crusaders and came to control the trade with the Orient. These colonies also allowed them to trade with the Eastern world. Though the fall of the Crusader states and attempts at banning of trade relations with Muslim states by the Popes temporarily disrupted the trade with the Orient, it however continued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>Europe started to revive, however, as more organized and centralized states began to form in the later <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_of_the_12th_century" title="Renaissance of the 12th century">Renaissance of the 12th century</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2061" data-file-width="2940" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/220px-thumbnail.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/330px-thumbnail.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/440px-thumbnail.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">bombardment of Algiers</a> by the Anglo-Dutch fleet in support of an ultimatum to release European slaves, August 1816</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> power based in Anatolia continued to grow, and in 1453 extinguished the Byzantine Empire with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Constantinople" title="Conquest of Constantinople">Conquest of Constantinople</a>. Ottomans gained control of much of the sea in the 16th century and maintained naval bases in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_occupation_of_Toulon" title="Ottoman occupation of Toulon">southern France</a> (1543–1544), Algeria and Tunisia. <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Barbarossa</a>, the famous Ottoman captain is a symbol of this domination with the victory of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Preveza" title="Battle of Preveza">Battle of Preveza</a> (1538). The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Djerba" title="Battle of Djerba">Battle of Djerba</a> (1560) marked the apex of Ottoman naval domination in the Mediterranean. As the naval prowess of the European powers increased, they confronted Ottoman expansion in the region when the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a> (1571) checked the power of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Navy" title="Ottoman Navy">Ottoman Navy</a>. This was the last naval battle to be fought primarily between <a href="/wiki/Galley" title="Galley">galleys</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwest_Africa" title="Northwest Africa">Northwest Africa</a> preyed on Christian shipping and coastlines in the Western Mediterranean Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> According to Robert Davis, from the 16th to 19th centuries, pirates captured 1 million to 1.25 million Europeans as slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>The development of oceanic shipping began to affect the entire Mediterranean. Once, most of the trade between Western Europe and the East was passing through the region, but after the 1490s the development of a sea route to the Indian Ocean allowed the importation of Asian <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spices</a> and other goods through the Atlantic ports of western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>The sea remained strategically important. British mastery of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> ensured their influence in Africa and Southwest Asia. Especially after the naval battles of Abukir (1799, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Nile" title="Battle of the Nile">Battle of the Nile</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Trafalgar</a> (1805), the British had for a long time strengthened their dominance in the Mediterranean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Wars included <a href="/wiki/Naval_warfare_in_the_Mediterranean_during_World_War_I" title="Naval warfare in the Mediterranean during World War I">Naval warfare in the Mediterranean during World War I</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="Mediterranean theatre of World War II">Mediterranean theatre of World War II</a>.
</p><p>With the opening of the lockless <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> in 1869, the flow of trade between Europe and Asia changed fundamentally. The fastest route now led through the Mediterranean towards East Africa and Asia. This led to a preference for the Mediterranean countries and their ports like <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a> with the direct connections to Central and Eastern Europe experienced a rapid economic rise. In the 20th century, the 1st and 2nd World War as well as the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> led to a shift of trade routes to the European northern ports, which changed again towards the southern ports through European integration, the activation of the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> and free world trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century_and_migrations">21st century and migrations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 21st century and migrations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_migrant_crisis" title="European migrant crisis">European migrant crisis</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_migrant_vessel_incidents_on_the_Mediterranean_Sea" title="List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea">List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_European_migrant_crisis" title="Timeline of the European migrant crisis">Timeline of the European migrant crisis</a></div><div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width: 272px;">
<div class="thumbimage" style="width: 270px; height: 110px; overflow: hidden;">
<div style="position: relative; top: -265px; left: -1055px; width: 2200px"><div class="noresize"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="21600" data-file-width="43200" decoding="async" height="1100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/2200px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/3300px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/4400px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg 2x" width="2200"/></a></div></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg" title="File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">Satellite image</a> of the Mediterranean Sea at night
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Maltese</a> president described the Mediterranean Sea as a "cemetery" due to the large number of migrants who drowned there after their boats capsized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> president <a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">Martin Schulz</a> said in 2014 that Europe's migration policy "turned the Mediterranean into a graveyard", referring to the number of drowned refugees in the region as a direct result of the policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> An Azerbaijani official described the sea as "a burial ground ... where people die".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2013_Lampedusa_migrant_shipwreck" title="2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck">2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Letta_Cabinet" title="Letta Cabinet">Italian government</a> decided to strengthen the national system for the patrolling of the Mediterranean Sea by authorising "<a href="/wiki/Operation_Mare_Nostrum" title="Operation Mare Nostrum">Operation Mare Nostrum</a>", a military and humanitarian mission in order to rescue the migrants and arrest the traffickers of immigrants. In 2015, more than one million migrants crossed the Mediterranean Sea into Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>Italy was particularly affected by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_migrant_crisis" title="European migrant crisis">European migrant crisis</a>. Since 2013, over 700,000 migrants have landed in Italy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> mainly sub-Saharan Africans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:368px;max-width:368px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="5222" data-file-width="5275" decoding="async" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg/270px-STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg/360px-STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">A satellite image showing the Mediterranean Sea. The <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> appears in the bottom left (north-west) quarter of the image; to its left is the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, and to its right, the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="653" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg/180px-Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg/270px-Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg/360px-Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">The <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkish_Straits" title="Turkish Straits">strait</a> in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. The north (upper) side forms part of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gelibolu_Peninsula" title="Gelibolu Peninsula">Gelibolu Peninsula</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a> region); on the south (lower) side is <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The Mediterranean Sea connects:
</p>
<ul><li>to the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> (known in <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">Homer</a>'s writings as the "<a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">Pillars of Hercules</a>") in the west</li>
<li>to the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, by the Straits of the <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bosporus" title="Bosporus">Bosporus</a> respectively, in the east</li></ul>
<p>The 163 km (101 mi) long artificial <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> in the southeast connects the Mediterranean Sea to the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> without ship lock, because the water level is essentially the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melitensia_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-melitensia-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>The westernmost point of the Mediterranean is located at the transition from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albor%C3%A1n_Sea" title="Alborán Sea">Alborán Sea</a> to the Strait of Gibraltar, the easternmost point is on the coast of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Iskenderun" title="Gulf of Iskenderun">Gulf of Iskenderun</a> in southeastern Turkey. The northernmost point of the Mediterranean is on the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Trieste" title="Gulf of Trieste">Gulf of Trieste</a> near <a href="/wiki/Monfalcone" title="Monfalcone">Monfalcone</a> in northern Italy while the southernmost point is on the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Sidra" title="Gulf of Sidra">Gulf of Sidra</a> near the Libyan town of <a href="/wiki/El_Agheila" title="El Agheila">El Agheila</a>.
</p><p>Large islands in the Mediterranean include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euboea" title="Euboea">Euboea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhodes" title="Rhodes">Rhodes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lesbos_Island" title="Lesbos Island">Lesbos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">Chios</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kefalonia" title="Kefalonia">Kefalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limnos" title="Limnos">Limnos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samos" title="Samos">Samos</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naxos_Island" title="Naxos Island">Naxos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andros" title="Andros">Andros</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean" title="Eastern Mediterranean">Eastern Mediterranean</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cres" title="Cres">Cres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krk" title="Krk">Krk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bra%C4%8D" title="Brač">Brač</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hvar" title="Hvar">Hvar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pag_(island)" title="Pag (island)">Pag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kor%C4%8Dula" title="Korčula">Korčula</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malta_Island" title="Malta Island">Malta</a> in the central Mediterranean</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>: <a href="/wiki/Ibiza" title="Ibiza">Ibiza</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">Majorca</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a> in the Western Mediterranean</li></ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alpine arc</a>, which also has a great meteorological impact on the Mediterranean area, touches the Mediterranean in the west in the area around <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a>.
</p><p>The typical <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> has hot, dry summers and mild, rainy winters. Crops of the region include <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tangerine" title="Tangerine">tangerines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carob" title="Carob">carobs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cork_(material)" title="Cork (material)">cork</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marginal_seas">Marginal seas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Marginal seas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</p><p>Note 3: The <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> is not considered part of it.

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent">Extent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Extent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_drainage_basins_by_area" title="List of drainage basins by area">List of drainage basins by area</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Locatie_Middellandse_Zee.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="551" data-file-width="902" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Locatie_Middellandse_Zee.PNG/220px-Locatie_Middellandse_Zee.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Locatie_Middellandse_Zee.PNG/330px-Locatie_Middellandse_Zee.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Locatie_Middellandse_Zee.PNG/440px-Locatie_Middellandse_Zee.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Locatie_Middellandse_Zee.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Borders of the Mediterranean Sea</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">International Hydrographic Organization</a> defines the limits of the Mediterranean Sea as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHO_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-IHO-30">[30]</a></sup> Stretching from the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> in the west to the entrances to the <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> in the east, the Mediterranean Sea is bounded by the coasts of Europe, Africa, and Asia and is divided into two deep basins:
</p>
<ul><li>Western Basin:
<ul><li>On the west: A line joining the extremities of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Trafalgar" title="Cape Trafalgar">Cape Trafalgar</a> (Spain) and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Spartel" title="Cape Spartel">Cape Spartel</a> (Africa)</li>
<li>On the northeast: The west coast of Italy. In the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Messina" title="Strait of Messina">Strait of Messina</a>, a line joining the north extreme of Cape Paci (15°42′E) with Cape Peloro, the east extreme of the Island of <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>. The north coast of Sicily</li>
<li>On the east: A line joining Cape Lilibeo the western point of Sicily (<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1073938472" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;params=37_47_N_12_22_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">37°47′N</span> <span class="longitude">12°22′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">37.783°N 12.367°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">37.783; 12.367</span></span></span></a></span>), through the Adventure Bank to <a href="/wiki/Cape_Bon" title="Cape Bon">Cape Bon</a> (Tunisia)</li></ul></li>
<li>Eastern Basin:
<ul><li>On the west: The northeastern and eastern limits of the Western Basin</li>
<li>On the northeast: A line joining <a href="/wiki/Kumkale,_%C3%87anakkale" title="Kumkale, Çanakkale">Kum Kale</a> (26°11′E) and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Helles" title="Cape Helles">Cape Helles</a>, the western entrance to the Dardanelles</li>
<li>On the southeast: The entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a></li>
<li>On the east: The coasts of <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">Hydrography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hydrography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mediterranean_Basin.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="923" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Mediterranean_Basin.png/220px-Mediterranean_Basin.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Mediterranean_Basin.png/330px-Mediterranean_Basin.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Mediterranean_Basin.png/440px-Mediterranean_Basin.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mediterranean_Basin.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Approximate extent of the Mediterranean drainage basin (dark green). <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a> basin only partially shown</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drainage basin</a> of the Mediterranean Sea is particularly heterogeneous and extends much further than the Mediterranean region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Its size has been estimated between 4,000,000 km<sup>2</sup> (1,500,000 sq mi) and 5,500,000 km<sup>2</sup> (2,100,000 sq mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[note 1]</a></sup> depending on whether non-active parts (deserts) are included or not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Margat_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Margat-34">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> The longest river ending in the Mediterranean Sea is the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a>, which takes its sources in equatorial Africa. The basin of the Nile constitutes about two-thirds of the Mediterranean drainage basin<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Margat_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Margat-34">[33]</a></sup>  and encompasses areas as high as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruwenzori_Mountains" title="Ruwenzori Mountains">Ruwenzori Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> Among other important rivers in Africa, are the <a href="/wiki/Moulouya_River" title="Moulouya River">Moulouya</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chelif_River" title="Chelif River">Chelif</a>, both on the north side of the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">Atlas Mountains</a>. In Asia, are the <a href="/wiki/Ceyhan_River" title="Ceyhan River">Ceyhan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seyhan_River" title="Seyhan River">Seyhan</a>, both on the south side of the <a href="/wiki/Taurus_Mountains" title="Taurus Mountains">Taurus Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNEP_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNEP-37">[36]</a></sup> In Europe, the largest basins are those of the <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B4ne" title="Rhône">Rhône</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Po_(river)" title="Po (river)">Po</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maritsa" title="Maritsa">Maritsa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNECE_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNECE-38">[37]</a></sup> The basin of the Rhône is the largest and extends up as far north as the <a href="/wiki/Jura_Mountains" title="Jura Mountains">Jura Mountains</a>, encompassing areas even on the north side of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> The basins of the Ebro, Po, and Maritsa, are respectively south of the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a>, Alps, and <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Mountains" title="Balkan Mountains">Balkan Mountains</a>, which are the major ranges bordering Southern Europe.
</p><p>Total annual precipitation is significantly higher on the European part of the Mediterranean basin, especially near the Alps (the 'water tower of Europe') and other high mountain ranges. As a consequence, the <a href="/wiki/Discharge_(hydrology)" title="Discharge (hydrology)">river discharges</a> of the Rhône and Po are similar to that of the Nile, despite the latter having a much larger basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNEP_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNEP-37">[36]</a></sup> These are the only three rivers with an average discharge of over 1,000 m<sup>3</sup>/s (35,000 cu ft/s).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Margat_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-Margat-34">[33]</a></sup> Among large natural fresh bodies of water are <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a> (Nile basin), <a href="/wiki/Lake_Geneva" title="Lake Geneva">Lake Geneva</a> (Rhône), and the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Lakes" title="Italian Lakes">Italian Lakes</a> (Po). While the Mediterranean watershed is bordered by other river basins in Europe, it is essentially bordered by <a href="/wiki/Endorheic_basin" title="Endorheic basin">endorheic basins</a> or deserts elsewhere.
</p><p>The following countries are in the Mediterranean drainage basin while <i>not</i> having a coastline on the Mediterranean Sea:
</p>
<ul><li>In Europe, through various rivers:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNECE_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNECE-38">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[note 2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[note 3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[note 4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[note 5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[note 6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[note 7]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[note 8]</a></sup></li></ul>
<ul><li>In Africa, through the Nile:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[40]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coastal_countries">Coastal countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Coastal countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mediterranean_countries" title="List of Mediterranean countries">List of Mediterranean countries</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Area_of_the_Mediterranean.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2699" data-file-width="5441" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Area_of_the_Mediterranean.jpg/300px-Area_of_the_Mediterranean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Area_of_the_Mediterranean.jpg/450px-Area_of_the_Mediterranean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Area_of_the_Mediterranean.jpg/600px-Area_of_the_Mediterranean.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Area_of_the_Mediterranean.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Mediterranean Sea from open Natural Earth data, 2020</div></div></div>
<p>The following countries have a coastline on the Mediterranean Sea:
</p>
<ul><li><b>Northern shore</b> (from west to east): <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.</li>
<li><b>Eastern shore</b> (from north to south): <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>.</li>
<li><b>Southern shore</b> (from west to east): <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>.</li>
<li><b>Island nations</b>: <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Several other territories also border the Mediterranean Sea (from west to east):
</p>
<ul><li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" title="British overseas territory">British overseas territory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a></li>
<li>the Spanish autonomous cities of <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plazas_de_soberan%C3%ADa" title="Plazas de soberanía">nearby islands</a></li>
<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovereign_Base_Areas" title="Sovereign Base Areas">Sovereign Base Areas</a> on Cyprus</li>
<li>the Palestinian <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_coast_(2715600220).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Alexandria_coast_%282715600220%29.jpg/220px-Alexandria_coast_%282715600220%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Alexandria_coast_%282715600220%29.jpg/330px-Alexandria_coast_%282715600220%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Alexandria_coast_%282715600220%29.jpg/440px-Alexandria_coast_%282715600220%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alexandria_coast_(2715600220).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, the largest city on the Mediterranean</div></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coastline_length">Coastline length</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Coastline length">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastline_length" title="Coastline length">Coastline length</a> is about 46,000 km.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coastal_cities">Coastal cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Coastal cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_coastal_settlements_of_the_Mediterranean_Sea" title="List of coastal settlements of the Mediterranean Sea">List of coastal settlements of the Mediterranean Sea</a>.</div>
<p>Major cities (municipalities), with populations larger than 200,000 people, bordering the Mediterranean Sea include:
</p>
<ul><li>Algeria: <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a></li>
<li>Egypt: <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damietta" title="Damietta">Damietta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Said" title="Port Said">Port Said</a></li>
<li>France: <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a></li>
<li>Greece: <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patras" title="Patras">Patras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heraklion" title="Heraklion">Heraklion</a></li>
<li>Israel: <a href="/wiki/Ashdod" title="Ashdod">Ashdod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netanya" title="Netanya">Netanya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rishon_LeZion" title="Rishon LeZion">Rishon LeZion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a></li>
<li>Italy: <a href="/wiki/Bari" title="Bari">Bari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catania" title="Catania">Catania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Messina" title="Messina">Messina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palermo" title="Palermo">Palermo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taranto" title="Taranto">Taranto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a></li>
<li>Lebanon: <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tripoli,_Lebanon" title="Tripoli, Lebanon">Tripoli</a></li>
<li>Libya: <a href="/wiki/Benghazi" title="Benghazi">Benghazi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Misrata" title="Misrata">Misrata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zawiya,_Libya" title="Zawiya, Libya">Zawiya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zliten" title="Zliten">Zliten</a></li>
<li>Malta: <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a></li>
<li>Morocco: <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9touan" title="Tétouan">Tétouan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a></li>
<li>Palestine: <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza City</a></li>
<li>Spain: <a href="/wiki/Alicante" title="Alicante">Alicante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almer%C3%ADa" title="Almería">Almería</a>, <a href="/wiki/Badalona" title="Badalona">Badalona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Spain" title="Cartagena, Spain">Cartagena</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">Málaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a>.</li>
<li>Syria: <a href="/wiki/Latakia" title="Latakia">Latakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tartus" title="Tartus">Tartus</a></li>
<li>Tunisia: <a href="/wiki/Sfax" title="Sfax">Sfax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sousse" title="Sousse">Sousse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a></li>
<li>Turkey: <a href="/wiki/Alanya" title="Alanya">Alanya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antalya" title="Antalya">Antalya</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%87anakkale" title="Çanakkale">Çanakkale</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0skenderun" title="İskenderun">İskenderun</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mersin" title="Mersin">Mersin</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="811" data-file-width="1208" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg/220px-Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg/330px-Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg/440px-Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Africa (left, on horizon) and Europe (right), as seen from Gibraltar</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">International Hydrographic Organization</a> (IHO) divides the Mediterranean into a number of smaller waterbodies, each with their own designation (from west to east):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHO_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-IHO-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Alboran_Sea" title="Alboran Sea">Alboran Sea</a>, between Spain and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Sea" title="Balearic Sea">Balearic Sea</a>, between mainland Spain and its <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Ligurian_Sea" title="Ligurian Sea">Ligurian Sea</a> between <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a> (Italy)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Tyrrhenian_Sea" title="Tyrrhenian Sea">Tyrrhenian Sea</a> enclosed by <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_peninsula" title="Italian peninsula">Italian peninsula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a> between Italy, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and Greece</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> between Italy, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> between Greece and Turkey</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_seas">Other seas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other seas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Positano_-_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2591" data-file-width="3870" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Positano_-_01.jpg/220px-Positano_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Positano_-_01.jpg/330px-Positano_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Positano_-_01.jpg/440px-Positano_-_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Positano_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Positano" title="Positano">Positano</a>, Italy, <a href="/wiki/Tyrrhenian_Sea" title="Tyrrhenian Sea">Tyrrhenian Sea</a></div></div></div>
<p>Some other seas whose names have been in common use from the ancient times, or in the present:
</p>
<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Sardinia" title="Sea of Sardinia">Sea of Sardinia</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>, as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Sea" title="Balearic Sea">Balearic Sea</a></li>
<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_of_Sicily" title="Sea of Sicily">Sea of Sicily</a> between <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Sea" title="Libyan Sea">Libyan Sea</a> between <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a></li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>,
<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Thracian_Sea" title="Thracian Sea">Thracian Sea</a> in its north</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Myrtoan_Sea" title="Myrtoan Sea">Myrtoan Sea</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Cyclades" title="Cyclades">Cyclades</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Peloponnese" title="Peloponnese">Peloponnese</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Crete" title="Sea of Crete">Sea of Crete</a> north of Crete</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Icarian_Sea" title="Icarian Sea">Icarian Sea</a> between <a href="/wiki/Kos" title="Kos">Kos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">Chios</a></li></ul></li>
<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cilician_Sea" title="Cilician Sea">Cilician Sea</a> between Turkey and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Levantine_Sea" title="Levantine Sea">Levantine Sea</a> at the eastern end of the Mediterranean</li></ul>
<p>Many of these smaller seas feature in local myth and folklore and derive their names from such associations.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_features">Other features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Other features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bey-Sannine-BCD.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Bey-Sannine-BCD.jpg/220px-Bey-Sannine-BCD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Bey-Sannine-BCD.jpg/330px-Bey-Sannine-BCD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Bey-Sannine-BCD.jpg/440px-Bey-Sannine-BCD.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bey-Sannine-BCD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_George_Bay" title="Saint George Bay">Saint George Bay</a>, and snow-capped <a href="/wiki/Mount_Sannine" title="Mount Sannine">Mount Sannine</a> from a tower in the <a href="/wiki/Beirut_Central_District" title="Beirut Central District">Beirut Central District</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Port_Autonome_de_Marseille.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Port_Autonome_de_Marseille.JPG/220px-Port_Autonome_de_Marseille.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Port_Autonome_de_Marseille.JPG/330px-Port_Autonome_de_Marseille.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Port_Autonome_de_Marseille.JPG/440px-Port_Autonome_de_Marseille.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Port_Autonome_de_Marseille.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Port of Marseille seen from <a href="/wiki/L%27Estaque" title="L'Estaque">L'Estaque</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CIty_of_Saranda_Albania_2016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3315" data-file-width="5472" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/CIty_of_Saranda_Albania_2016.jpg/220px-CIty_of_Saranda_Albania_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/CIty_of_Saranda_Albania_2016.jpg/330px-CIty_of_Saranda_Albania_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/CIty_of_Saranda_Albania_2016.jpg/440px-CIty_of_Saranda_Albania_2016.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CIty_of_Saranda_Albania_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sarand%C3%AB" title="Sarandë">Sarandë</a>, Albania, stands on an open-sea gulf of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ionian_sea" title="Ionian sea">Ionian sea</a> in the central Mediterranean.</div></div></div>
<p>In addition to the seas, a number of gulfs and <a href="/wiki/Strait" title="Strait">straits</a> are recognised:
</p>
<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Saint_George_Bay" title="Saint George Bay">Saint George Bay</a> in Beirut, Lebanon</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Ras_Ibn_Hani" title="Ras Ibn Hani">Ras Ibn Hani</a> cape in <a href="/wiki/Latakia" title="Latakia">Latakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Ras_al-Bassit" title="Ras al-Bassit">Ras al-Bassit</a> cape in northern Syria.</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Minet_el-Beida" title="Minet el-Beida">Minet el-Beida</a> ("White Harbour") bay near ancient <a href="/wiki/Ugarit" title="Ugarit">Ugarit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>, connects the Atlantic Ocean to the Mediterranean Sea and separates Spain from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a></li>
<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bay_of_Algeciras" title="Bay of Algeciras">Bay of Algeciras</a>, at the southern end of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Corinth" title="Gulf of Corinth">Gulf of Corinth</a>, an enclosed sea between the Ionian Sea and the <a href="/wiki/Corinth_Canal" title="Corinth Canal">Corinth Canal</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Pagasetic_Gulf" title="Pagasetic Gulf">Pagasetic Gulf</a>, the gulf of <a href="/wiki/Volos" title="Volos">Volos</a>, south of the Thermaic Gulf, formed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Pelion" title="Mount Pelion">Mount Pelion</a> <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Saronic_Gulf" title="Saronic Gulf">Saronic Gulf</a>, the gulf of <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, between the Corinth Canal and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mirtoan_Sea" title="Mirtoan Sea">Mirtoan Sea</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Thermaic_Gulf" title="Thermaic Gulf">Thermaic Gulf</a>, the gulf of <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, located in the northern Greek region of <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(Greece)" title="Macedonia (Greece)">Macedonia</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Kvarner_Gulf" title="Kvarner Gulf">Kvarner Gulf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a></li>
<li>the Gulf of Almeria, southeast of Spain</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Lion" title="Gulf of Lion">Gulf of Lion</a>, south of France</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Valencia" title="Gulf of Valencia">Gulf of Valencia</a>, east of Spain</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Messina" title="Strait of Messina">Strait of Messina</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">Calabrian</a> peninsula</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Genoa" title="Gulf of Genoa">Gulf of Genoa</a>, northwestern Italy</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Venice" title="Gulf of Venice">Gulf of Venice</a>, northeastern Italy</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Trieste" title="Gulf of Trieste">Gulf of Trieste</a>, northeastern Italy</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Taranto" title="Gulf of Taranto">Gulf of Taranto</a>, southern Italy</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Euphemia" title="Gulf of Saint Euphemia">Gulf of Saint Euphemia</a>, southern Italy, with the international airport nearby</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Salerno" title="Gulf of Salerno">Gulf of Salerno</a>, southwestern Italy</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Gaeta" title="Gulf of Gaeta">Gulf of Gaeta</a>, southwestern Italy</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Squillace" title="Gulf of Squillace">Gulf of Squillace</a>, southern Italy</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Otranto" title="Strait of Otranto">Strait of Otranto</a>, between Italy and <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a></li>
<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Haifa" title="Gulf of Haifa">Gulf of Haifa</a>, northern Israel</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Sidra" title="Gulf of Sidra">Gulf of Sidra</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Tripolitania" title="Tripolitania">Tripolitania</a> (western Libya) and <a href="/wiki/Cyrenaica" title="Cyrenaica">Cyrenaica</a> (eastern Libya)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Sicily" title="Strait of Sicily">Strait of Sicily</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a></li>
<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corsica_Channel" title="Corsica Channel">Corsica Channel</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> and Italy</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Bonifacio" title="Strait of Bonifacio">Strait of Bonifacio</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Antalya" title="Gulf of Antalya">Gulf of Antalya</a>, between west and east shores of Antalya (Turkey)</li>
<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_of_%C4%B0skenderun" title="Gulf of İskenderun">Gulf of İskenderun</a>, between <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0skenderun" title="İskenderun">İskenderun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adana" title="Adana">Adana</a> (Turkey)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_%C4%B0zmir" title="Gulf of İzmir">Gulf of İzmir</a>, in <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a> (Turkey)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Fethiye" title="Gulf of Fethiye">Gulf of Fethiye</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Fethiye" title="Fethiye">Fethiye</a> (Turkey)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Ku%C5%9Fadas%C4%B1" title="Gulf of Kuşadası">Gulf of Kuşadası</a>, in <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a> (Turkey)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Kotor" title="Bay of Kotor">Bay of Kotor</a>, in south-western <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> and south-eastern <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Malta_Channel" title="Malta Channel">Malta Channel</a>, between Sicily and Malta</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gozo_Channel" title="Gozo Channel">Gozo Channel</a>, between Malta Island and <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_islands">Largest islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Largest islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_in_the_Mediterranean" title="List of islands in the Mediterranean">List of islands in the Mediterranean</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tunisia_-_Sicily_-_South_Italy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="699" data-file-width="1002" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Tunisia_-_Sicily_-_South_Italy.jpg/220px-Tunisia_-_Sicily_-_South_Italy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Tunisia_-_Sicily_-_South_Italy.jpg/330px-Tunisia_-_Sicily_-_South_Italy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Tunisia_-_Sicily_-_South_Italy.jpg/440px-Tunisia_-_Sicily_-_South_Italy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tunisia_-_Sicily_-_South_Italy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The two biggest islands of the Mediterranean: <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>)</div></div></div>

</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Much of the Mediterranean coast enjoys a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate#Hot-summer_Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">hot-summer Mediterranean climate</a>. However, most of its southeastern coast has a <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate#Hot_desert_climates" title="Desert climate">hot desert climate</a>, and much of Spain's eastern (Mediterranean) coast has a <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate#Cold_semi-arid_climates" title="Semi-arid climate">cold semi-arid climate</a>, while most of Italy's northern (Adriatic) coast has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a>. Although they are rare, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_tropical-like_cyclone" title="Mediterranean tropical-like cyclone">tropical cyclones occasionally form in the Mediterranean Sea</a>, typically in September–November.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:777px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_(Mediterranean_Sea_area_only).png" title="Map of climate zones in the areas surrounding the Mediterranean Sea, according to the Köppen climate classification"><img alt="" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="769" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f8/Koppen_World_Map_%28Mediterranean_Sea_area_only%29.png" width="769"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_(Mediterranean_Sea_area_only).png" title="File:Koppen World Map (Mediterranean Sea area only).png"> </a></div>Map of climate zones in the areas surrounding the Mediterranean Sea, according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a></div></div></div>
