<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceanography">Oceanography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Oceanography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MEDCURR.GIF"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="250" data-file-width="497" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/MEDCURR.GIF/360px-MEDCURR.GIF" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ef/MEDCURR.GIF 1.5x" width="360"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MEDCURR.GIF" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Predominant surface currents for June</div></div></div>
<p>Being nearly landlocked affects conditions in the Mediterranean Sea: for instance, <a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">tides</a> are very limited as a result of the narrow connection with the Atlantic Ocean. The Mediterranean is characterised and immediately recognised by its deep blue colour.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Evaporation" title="Evaporation">Evaporation</a> greatly exceeds <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> and river runoff in the Mediterranean, a fact that is central to the water circulation within the basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[61]</a></sup> Evaporation is especially high in its eastern half, causing the water level to decrease and <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">salinity</a> to increase eastward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[62]</a></sup> The average salinity in the basin is 38 <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">PSU</a> at 5 m depth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tempandsal_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-tempandsal-71">[63]</a></sup>
The temperature of the water in the deepest part of the Mediterranean Sea is 13.2 °C (55.8 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tempandsal_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-tempandsal-71">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>The net water influx from the Atlantic Ocean is ca. 70,000 m³/s or 2.2<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>12</sup> m<sup>3</sup>/a (7.8<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>13</sup> cu ft/a).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[64]</a></sup> Without this Atlantic water, the sea level of the Mediterranean Sea would fall at a rate of about  1 m per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_circulation">General circulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: General circulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_circulation" title="Water circulation">Water circulation</a> in the Mediterranean can be attributed to the surface waters entering from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> (and also low salinity water entering the Mediterranean from the Black Sea through the Bosphorus). The cool and relatively low-salinity Atlantic water circulates eastwards along the North African coasts. A part of the surface water does not pass the Strait of Sicily, but deviates towards <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> before exiting the Mediterranean. The surface waters entering the eastern Mediterranean basin circulate along the Libyan and Israeli coasts. Upon reaching the <a href="/wiki/Levantine_Sea" title="Levantine Sea">Levantine Sea</a>, the surface waters having warmed and increased its salinity from its initial Atlantic state, is now denser and sinks to form the Levantine Intermediate Waters (LIW). Most of the water found anywhere between 50 and 600 m deep in the Mediterranean originates from the LIW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[66]</a></sup> LIW are formed along the coasts of Turkey and circulate westwards along the Greek and South Italian coasts. LIW are the only waters passing the Sicily Strait westwards. After the Strait of Sicily, the LIW waters circulate along the Italian, French and Spanish coasts before exiting the Mediterranean through the depths of the Strait of Gibraltar. Deep water in the Mediterranean originates from three main areas: the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a>, from which most of the deep water in the eastern Mediterranean originates, the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Lion" title="Gulf of Lion">Gulf of Lion</a>. Deep water formation in the Mediterranean is triggered by strong winter <a href="/wiki/Convection" title="Convection">convection</a> fueled by intense cold winds like the <a href="/wiki/Bora_(wind)" title="Bora (wind)">Bora</a>. When new deep water is formed, the older waters mix with the overlaying intermediate waters and eventually exit the Mediterranean. The <a href="/wiki/Water_cycle#Residence_times" title="Water cycle">residence time of water</a> in the Mediterranean is approximately 100 years, making the Mediterranean especially sensitive to climate change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_events_affecting_water_circulation">Other events affecting water circulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other events affecting water circulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Being a semi-enclosed basin, the Mediterranean experiences transitory events that can affect the water circulation on short time scales. In the mid 1990s, the Aegean Sea became the main area for deep water formation in the eastern Mediterranean after particularly cold winter conditions. This transitory switch in the origin of deep waters in the eastern Mediterranean was termed Eastern Mediterranean Transient (EMT) and had major consequences on water circulation of the Mediterranean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[70]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another example of a transient event affecting the Mediterranean circulation is the periodic inversion of the North Ionian Gyre, which is an <a href="/wiki/Anticyclonic_rotation" title="Anticyclonic rotation">anticyclonic</a> <a href="/wiki/Ocean_gyre" title="Ocean gyre">ocean gyre</a> observed in the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a>, off the Greek coast. The transition from anticyclonic to cyclonic rotation of this gyre changes the origin of the waters fueling it; when the circulation is anticyclonic (most common), the waters of the gyre originate from the Adriatic Sea. When the circulation is cyclonic, the waters originate from the <a href="/wiki/Levantine_Sea" title="Levantine Sea">Levantine Sea</a>. These waters have different physical and chemical characteristics, and the periodic inversion of the North Ionian Gyre (called Bimodal Oscillating System or BiOS) changes the Mediterranean circulation and biogeochemistry around the Adriatic and Levantine regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Because of the short residence time of waters, the Mediterranean Sea is considered a hot-spot for climate change effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Giorgi,_F._2006_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Giorgi,_F._2006-80">[72]</a></sup> Deep water temperatures have increased by 0.12 °C (0.22 °F) between 1959 and 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[73]</a></sup> According to climate projections, the Mediterranean Sea could become warmer. The decrease in precipitation over the region could lead to more evaporation ultimately increasing the Mediterranean Sea salinity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Giorgi,_F._2006_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-Giorgi,_F._2006-80">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[74]</a></sup> Because of the changes in temperature and salinity, the Mediterranean Sea may become more stratified by the end of the 21st century, with notable consequences on water circulation and <a href="/wiki/Biogeochemistry" title="Biogeochemistry">biogeochemistry</a>. The stratification and warming have already led to the eastern Mediterranean to become a net source of CO<sub>2</sub> to the atmosphere <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[75]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[76]</a></sup> notably during summer. This strong summer degassing, combined with the prolonged and pronounced stratification results in the formation of <a href="/wiki/Aragonite" title="Aragonite">aragonite</a> crystals abiotically in the water column.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[77]</a></sup> The cumulative warming at the surface of the Mediterranean has a significant impact on the ecological system. Extreme warming has lead to biodiversity loss <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[78]</a></sup> and presents an existential threat to some habitats <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[79]</a></sup> while making conditions more hospitable to invasive tropical species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biogeochemistry">Biogeochemistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Biogeochemistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In spite of its great <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, concentrations of <a href="/wiki/Chlorophyll" title="Chlorophyll">chlorophyll</a> and nutrients in the Mediterranean Sea are very low, making it one of the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oligotrophic" title="Oligotrophic">oligotrophic</a> ocean regions in the world. The Mediterranean Sea is commonly referred to as an LNLC (Low-Nutrient, Low-Chlorophyll) area. The Mediterranean Sea fits the definition of a <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a> in which its nutrient contents are low, making it difficult for plants and animals to develop.
</p><p>There are steep gradients in nutrient concentrations, chlorophyll concentrations and primary productivity in the Mediterranean. Nutrient concentrations in the western part of the basin are about double the concentrations in the eastern basin. The <a href="/wiki/Alboran_Sea" title="Alboran Sea">Alboran Sea</a>, close to the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>, has a daily <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_productivity" title="Primary productivity">primary productivity</a> of about 0.25 g C (grams of carbon) m<sup>−2</sup> day<sup>−1</sup> whereas the eastern basin has an average daily productivity of 0.16 g C m<sup>−2</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[81]</a></sup> For this reason, the eastern part of the Mediterranean Sea is termed "ultraoligotrophic". The productive areas of the Mediterranean Sea are few and small. High (i.e. more than 0.5 grams of <a href="/wiki/Chlorophyll_a" title="Chlorophyll a">Chlorophyll <i>a</i></a> per cubic meter) productivity occurs in coastal areas, close to the river mouths which are the primary suppliers of dissolved nutrients. The <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Lion" title="Gulf of Lion">Gulf of Lion</a> has a relatively high productivity because it is an area of high vertical mixing, bringing nutrients to the surface waters that can be used by <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">phytoplankton</a> to produce Chlorophyll <i>a</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bosc,_E._2004_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bosc,_E._2004-90">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>Primary productivity in the Mediterranean is also marked by an intense seasonal variability. In winter, the strong winds and precipitation over the basin generate <a href="/wiki/Convective_mixing" title="Convective mixing">vertical mixing</a>, bringing nutrients from the deep waters to the surface, where phytoplankton can convert it into <a href="/wiki/Biomass_(ecology)" title="Biomass (ecology)">biomass</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[83]</a></sup> However, in winter, light may be the limiting factor for primary productivity. Between March and April, spring offers the ideal trade-off between light intensity and nutrient concentrations in surface for a <a href="/wiki/Spring_bloom" title="Spring bloom">spring bloom</a> to occur. In summer, high atmospheric temperatures lead to the warming of the surface waters. The resulting <a href="/wiki/Density" title="Density">density</a> difference virtually isolates the surface waters from the rest of the water column and nutrient exchanges are limited. As a consequence, primary productivity is very low between June and October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bosc,_E._2004_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bosc,_E._2004-90">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>Oceanographic expeditions uncovered a characteristic feature of the Mediterranean Sea biogeochemistry: most of the chlorophyll production does not occur on the surface, but in sub-surface waters between 80 and 200 meters deep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[85]</a></sup> Another key characteristic of the Mediterranean is its high nitrogen-to-phosphorus ratio (N:P). <a href="/wiki/Alfred_C._Redfield" title="Alfred C. Redfield">Redfield</a> demonstrated that most of the world's oceans have an average N:P ratio around 16. However, the Mediterranean Sea has an average N:P between 24 and 29, which translates a widespread phosphorus limitation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>Because of its low productivity, plankton assemblages in the Mediterranean Sea are dominated by small organisms such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Picophytoplankton" title="Picophytoplankton">picophytoplankton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[91]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geology_and_paleoclimatology_of_the_Mediterranean_Basin" title="Geology and paleoclimatology of the Mediterranean Basin">Geology and paleoclimatology of the Mediterranean Basin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg/220px-Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg/330px-Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg/440px-Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A submarine <a href="/wiki/Karst_spring" title="Karst spring">karst spring</a>, called <i>vrulja</i>, near <a href="/wiki/Omi%C5%A1" title="Omiš">Omiš</a>; observed through several ripplings of an otherwise calm sea surface.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geologic history</a> of the Mediterranean Sea is complex. Underlain by <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_crust" title="Oceanic crust">oceanic crust</a>, the sea basin was once thought to be a tectonic remnant of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Tethys_Ocean" title="Tethys Ocean">Tethys Ocean</a>; it is now known to be a structurally younger basin, called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neotethys" title="Neotethys">Neotethys</a>, which was first formed by the convergence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_plate" title="African plate">African</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurasian_plate" title="Eurasian plate">Eurasian plates</a> during the Late <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a> and Early <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a>. Because it is a near-landlocked body of water in a normally dry climate, the Mediterranean is subject to intensive evaporation and the precipitation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evaporites" title="Evaporites">evaporites</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Messinian_salinity_crisis" title="Messinian salinity crisis">Messinian salinity crisis</a> started about six million years ago (mya) when the Mediterranean became landlocked, and then essentially dried up. There are salt deposits accumulated on the bottom of the basin of more than a million cubic kilometres—in some places more than three kilometres thick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>Scientists estimate that the sea was last filled about 5.3 million years ago (mya) in less than two years by the <a href="/wiki/Zanclean_flood" title="Zanclean flood">Zanclean flood</a>. Water poured in from the Atlantic Ocean through a newly breached gateway now called the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> at an estimated rate of about three orders of magnitude (one thousand times) larger than the current flow of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCetal2009_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCetal2009-102">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Mediterranean Sea has an average depth of 1,500 m (4,900 ft) and the deepest recorded point is 5,267 m (17,280 ft) in the <a href="/wiki/Calypso_Deep" title="Calypso Deep">Calypso Deep</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a>. The coastline extends for 46,000 km (29,000 mi). A shallow submarine ridge (the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Sicily" title="Strait of Sicily">Strait of Sicily</a>) between the island of <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and the coast of <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> divides the sea in two main subregions: the Western Mediterranean, with an area of about 850,000 km<sup>2</sup> (330,000 mi<sup>2</sup>); and the Eastern Mediterranean, of about 1.65 million km<sup>2</sup> (640,000 mi<sup>2</sup>). Coastal areas have submarine <a href="/wiki/Karst_spring" title="Karst spring">karst springs</a> or <span title="Croatian-language text"><i lang="hr">vrulja</i></span>s, which discharge pressurised groundwater into the water from below the surface; the discharge water is usually fresh, and sometimes may be thermal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaMoreaux2001_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaMoreaux2001-103">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tectonics_and_paleoenvironmental_analysis">Tectonics and paleoenvironmental analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Tectonics and paleoenvironmental analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2018</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The Mediterranean basin and sea system were established by the ancient African-Arabian continent colliding with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurasian" title="Eurasian">Eurasian</a> continent. As Africa-Arabia drifted northward, it closed over the ancient <a href="/wiki/Tethys_Ocean" title="Tethys Ocean">Tethys Ocean</a> which had earlier separated the two supercontinents <a href="/wiki/Laurasia" title="Laurasia">Laurasia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">Gondwana</a>.
At about that time in the middle <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> period (roughly 170 million years ago<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (November 2018)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Mediterranean_Sea#Dubious" title="Talk:Mediterranean Sea">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup>) a much smaller sea basin, dubbed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neotethys" title="Neotethys">Neotethys</a>, was formed shortly before the Tethys Ocean closed at its western (Arabian) end. The broad line of collisions pushed up a very long system of mountains from the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> in Spain to the <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">Zagros Mountains</a> in Iran in an episode of mountain-building tectonics known as the <a href="/wiki/Alpine_orogeny" title="Alpine orogeny">Alpine orogeny</a>. The Neotethys grew larger during the episodes of collisions (and associated foldings and subductions) that occurred during the <a href="/wiki/Oligocene" title="Oligocene">Oligocene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a> epochs (34 to 5.33 mya); see animation: <a href="/wiki/Supercontinent" title="Supercontinent">Africa-Arabia colliding with Eurasia</a>. Accordingly, the Mediterranean <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_basin" title="Oceanic basin">basin</a> consists of several stretched <a href="/wiki/Tectonics" title="Tectonics">tectonic</a> plates in <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">subduction</a> which are the foundation of the eastern part of the Mediterranean Sea. Various zones of subduction contain the highest oceanic ridges, east of the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a> and south of the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Indian_Ridge" title="Central Indian Ridge">Central Indian Ridge</a> runs east of the Mediterranean Sea south-east across the in-between<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Messinian_salinity_crisis">Messinian salinity crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Messinian salinity crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Etapa3muda.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2195" data-file-width="3246" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Etapa3muda.jpg/260px-Etapa3muda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Etapa3muda.jpg/390px-Etapa3muda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Etapa3muda.jpg/520px-Etapa3muda.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Etapa3muda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Messinian salinity crisis before the <a href="/wiki/Zanclean_flood" title="Zanclean flood">Zanclean flood</a></div></div></div>
