<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLionello,_P.2012">Lionello, P. (2012). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=a2u4HMfAMXoC" rel="nofollow"><i>The Climate of the Mediterranean Region: From the Past to the Future</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Elsevier" title="Elsevier">Elsevier</a>. p. lxii. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780123914774" title="Special:BookSources/9780123914774"><bdi>9780123914774</bdi></a>. <q>Geographically, the Mediterranean catchment is extremely large and heterogeneous, covering an area of approximately 5 millions km<sup>2</sup>. It extends from the equator, where the springs of the White Nile River are located, to the source of the Rhone River at approximately 48°N. In longitude, it spans about 40°, from the middle of the Iberian peninsula, at 4°W, towards southern Turkey and the Middle East coasts facing the Mediterranean Sea (35°E).</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Climate+of+the+Mediterranean+Region%3A+From+the+Past+to+the+Future&amp;rft.pages=lxii&amp;rft.pub=Elsevier&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.isbn=9780123914774&amp;rft.au=Lionello%2C+P.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Da2u4HMfAMXoC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMediterranean+Sea"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFPoulos,_Serafeim2011">Poulos, Serafeim (2011). "An insight to the fluvial characteristics of the Mediterranean and Black Sea watersheds". <a class="external text" href="https://www.researchgate.net/publication/226665381" rel="nofollow"><i>Advances in the Research of Aquatic Environment</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Springer_Nature" title="Springer Nature">Springer Nature</a>. p. 191. <q>The drainage basin of the Mediterranean Sea, accounting for some 4,184 10<sup>3</sup> km<sup>2</sup> (including the R. Nile)</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=An+insight+to+the+fluvial+characteristics+of+the+Mediterranean+and+Black+Sea+watersheds&amp;rft.btitle=Advances+in+the+Research+of+Aquatic+Environment&amp;rft.pages=191&amp;rft.pub=Springer+Nature&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.au=Poulos%2C+Serafeim&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.researchgate.net%2Fpublication%2F226665381&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMediterranean+Sea"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Margat-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Margat_34-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Margat_34-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Margat_34-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFMargat,_Jean_F.2004">Margat, Jean F. (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=n5CGAAAAIAAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Mediterranean Basin Water Atlas</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>. p. 4. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9782951718159" title="Special:BookSources/9782951718159"><bdi>9782951718159</bdi></a>. <q>A basin of varied geometry: Area of the entire Mediterranean Basin, including the whole of the Nile Basin = 4,562,480 km<sup>2</sup>; Area of the 'conventional' Mediterranean Basin (i.e. counting only part of the Nile Basin in Egypt) = 1,836,480 km<sup>2</sup> [...] There are few rivers with an abundant flow. Only three rivers have a mean discharge of more than 1000 m<sup>3</sup>/s: the Nile (at Aswan), the Rhône and the Po.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Mediterranean+Basin+Water+Atlas&amp;rft.pages=4&amp;rft.pub=UNESCO&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=9782951718159&amp;rft.au=Margat%2C+Jean+F.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dn5CGAAAAIAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMediterranean+Sea"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFGarcía-García,_D.2022">García-García, D. (2022). <a class="external text" href="https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s00382-022-06188-2" rel="nofollow">"Hydrological cycle of the Mediterranean-Black Sea system"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Climate_Dynamics" title="Climate Dynamics">Climate Dynamics</a></i>. <b>59</b> (7–8): 1919–1938. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier)" title="Bibcode (identifier)">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2022ClDy...59.1919G" rel="nofollow">2022ClDy...59.1919G</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1007%2Fs00382-022-06188-2" rel="nofollow">10.1007/s00382-022-06188-2</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:247013753" rel="nofollow">247013753</a>. <q>In the continents, the drainage basins discharging into the Mediterranean and Black seas are defined according to the global continental runoff pathways scheme (Oki and Sud 1998), and they cover 5.34 × 10<sup>6</sup> and 2.43 × 10<sup>6</sup> km<sup>2</sup>, respectively</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Climate+Dynamics&amp;rft.atitle=Hydrological+cycle+of+the+Mediterranean-Black+Sea+system&amp;rft.volume=59&amp;rft.issue=7%E2%80%938&amp;rft.pages=1919-1938&amp;rft.date=2022&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A247013753%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1007%2Fs00382-022-06188-2&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F2022ClDy...59.1919G&amp;rft.au=Garc%C3%ADa-Garc%C3%ADa%2C+D.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Flink.springer.com%2Farticle%2F10.1007%2Fs00382-022-06188-2&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMediterranean+Sea"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFGupta,_Avijit2008">Gupta, Avijit (2008). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gXgyHLT_hwIC" rel="nofollow"><i>Large Rivers: Geomorphology and Management</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Wiley_%26_Sons" title="John Wiley &amp; Sons">John Wiley &amp; Sons</a>. p. 275. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780470723715" title="Special:BookSources/9780470723715"><bdi>9780470723715</bdi></a>. <q>The highest point in the Nile basin is Mount Stanley (5109 m) in the Ruwenzori Mountain range between Lake Edward and Lake Albert</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Large+Rivers%3A+Geomorphology+and+Management&amp;rft.pages=275&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.isbn=9780470723715&amp;rft.au=Gupta%2C+Avijit&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DgXgyHLT_hwIC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMediterranean+Sea"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-UNEP-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-UNEP_37-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-UNEP_37-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.medqsr.org/mediterranean-marine-and-coastal-environment" rel="nofollow">"The Mediterranean Marine and Coastal Environment: Hydrological and climatic setting"</a>. <li id="cite_note-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-48">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.rti.org/impact/nile-river-basin-initiative" rel="nofollow">"The Nile River Basin Initiative"</a>. <a href="/wiki/RTI_International" title="RTI International">RTI International</a>. 23 May 2018<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">14 March</span> 2022</span>. <q>The longest river in the world, the Nile spans 35 degrees of latitude, drains three million square kilometers of land (one-tenth of the total surface area of Africa), and runs through 11 countries whose combined population totals over 300 million people: Egypt, Ethiopia, Eritrea, Kenya, Rwanda, Burundi, Tanzania, Uganda, Sudan, South Sudan, and the Democratic Republic of the Congo. The Nile’s primary water source, Lake Victoria, is the world’s second-largest body of fresh water, and the Nile Delta in northern Egypt covers over 150 miles of the Mediterranean coastline.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=The+Nile+River+Basin+Initiative&amp;rft.pub=RTI+International&amp;rft.date=2018-05-23&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.rti.org%2Fimpact%2Fnile-river-basin-initiative&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMediterranean+Sea"></span></span>
